<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText3270560366618065110" style="display:none">بعد خمس سنوات من العُزلة الاختيارية يستأنف د. يحيى عمله في مستشفى العباسية للصحّة النفسية، حيث يجد في انتظاره مفاجأة..<br /><br />في "8 غرب"، القسم الذي يقرّر مَصير مُرتكبي الجرائم، يُقابل صديقاً قديماً يحمل إليه ماضياً جاهد طويلاً لينساه، ويصبح مَصيره فجأة بين يدي يحيى..<br /><br />تعصِف المفاجآت بيحيى وتنقلب حياته رأسًا على عقب، ليصبح ما بدأ كمحاولة لاكتشاف حقيقة صديقه، رحلة مثيرة لاكتشاف نفسه.. أو ما تبقى منها..<br /><br />يأخذنا أحمد مراد في روايته الثالثة إلى كواليس عالم غريب قضى عامين في دراسة تفاصيله، رحلة مثيرة مستكشف فيها أعمق وأغرب خبايا النفس البشرية..</span>

Regret can be a very powerful enemy that could not only shackles you but drag you down to the deepest pits of hell and make you do despicable things!! But, It can also be your guide about what really matters to you the most in life!!<br />Read it, It is not like any other thing you read..</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8015185678418805987">Perfect! perfect! Although quite non-traditional for Ahmed Mourad to explore this genre of writing but, as expected, he excelled at it. The novel starts as if it is following the traditional crime <br/>lines followed in Vertigo and "Torab El Mas" but takes a completely different and more exciting twist while progressing. <br/>What I didn't like is the excessive use of drinking, drugs and sex (although quite essential for the plot and is really used very cleverly).<br/>In short, really immersing novel, REALLY s</span>
  <span id="freeText8015185678418805987" style="display:none">Perfect! perfect! Although quite non-traditional for Ahmed Mourad to explore this genre of writing but, as expected, he excelled at it. The novel starts as if it is following the traditional crime <br />lines followed in Vertigo and "Torab El Mas" but takes a completely different and more exciting twist while progressing. <br />What I didn't like is the excessive use of drinking, drugs and sex (although quite essential for the plot and is really used very cleverly).<br />In short, really immersing novel, REALLY scary, exciting and unexpected. Couldn't leave it before finishing it, which I did in exactly two days. Highly recommended! </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer551841056" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9104423373155273207">WHAT THE HELL DID I JUST READ!!!<br/><br/>I like Ahmed Mourad he is the one of the few Arabic authors whom i read for. As usual his style in writing remained unchanged,it was full of his usual humor and the ugly truth. It was a very easy read I finished it in a day and a half, even though to be honest I did skip few useless paragraphs. <br/><br/>Now to the story it's self.<br/>It's very gripping.. it makes you not wanting to put down the book until you know what the hell is going on!<br/><br/>I think that he wanted to turn an old</span>
  <span id="freeText9104423373155273207" style="display:none">WHAT THE HELL DID I JUST READ!!!<br /><br />I like Ahmed Mourad he is the one of the few Arabic authors whom i read for. As usual his style in writing remained unchanged,it was full of his usual humor and the ugly truth. It was a very easy read I finished it in a day and a half, even though to be honest I did skip few useless paragraphs. <br /><br />Now to the story it's self.<br />It's very gripping.. it makes you not wanting to put down the book until you know what the hell is going on!<br /><br />I think that he wanted to turn an old burned story in movies and books and add his little touch and twist to it and he ended up with this modified cliche. <br /><br />I was very confused with the images of the characters, he draws them this American lifestyle, picking up the mail from the front door, the garden, the shoes kicking and the fish tub and then he switches to this Egyptian version of them where I just couldn't put my hands on the looks of them. He is very inspired by the American lifestyle which don't really go with the pure Egyptian story he is making, or maybe cause his stories are always translated to other foreign languages, he was trying keep them connected or something. <br /><br />Now, He always leaves me disappointed with his endings, they keep getting better I admit but still there is lots of room to grow.<br /><br />I was also disappointed with him for not reveling enough information at the end, like what happened to Maya?! he never showed us that.<br />Also what happened to Sherif, he could have spent a little time on how much control did he have with Na'el and their battle, it would have been interesting to know.<br /><br />Over-all I had a good time with the novel and am not judging the whole ghosty aspect of it .. I don't wanna upset any " spirit " out there =D </span>
  <a data-text-id="9104423373155273207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer819668571626621791">before reviewing this novel,,this is NOT a YA, its content as writing , twist and language wont be suitable for 20 and younger.<br/><br/>having that said..now reviewing the novel<br/><br/>This novel will easily take your brain put it in a washing-machine, and Ta-daaaaa your mind will be out as white as a rainbow.<br/><br/>the writing is very colorful, vivid , imaginative, and descriptive.<br/>the plot is a page turner, and although it might be little predicative, still you will be faced with a a worthy good twist.<br/><br/><br/>as for the main </span>
  <span id="freeText819668571626621791" style="display:none">before reviewing this novel,,this is NOT a YA, its content as writing , twist and language wont be suitable for 20 and younger.<br /><br />having that said..now reviewing the novel<br /><br />This novel will easily take your brain put it in a washing-machine, and Ta-daaaaa your mind will be out as white as a rainbow.<br /><br />the writing is very colorful, vivid , imaginative, and descriptive.<br />the plot is a page turner, and although it might be little predicative, still you will be faced with a a worthy good twist.<br /><br /><br />as for the main protagonists,not the kind you cheer for, I dont know about other readers, but I wasn't attached NOR sympathized with him. and I think that was kinda of the point, you dont care about the protagonist more than wanting to know the TRUTH behind it.<br /><br />one thing that noticed is the author making all his chr. bad. without morals, but you cant expect less when the protagonist IS moral-less guy, cant help to notice though,the author's comment at the end of the pages when he categorized the people, describing one in particular with genuine unlikeness,as if there is pure hatred for anything that might be good.<br /><br />all in all , a very good novel, minding the whole rudeness woven in it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2562256966221177353">Although "Diamond Dust" remains my favourite Ahmed Mourad piece, this book, like all his other books, is outstanding! In this book, Mourad takes us to the Al-Abbaseyya mental hospital in Cairo where Dr Yahia goes back to pursue his work after staying at home willingly for 5 years. He happens to meet an old friend, Sherif, who comes as a murderer accused of murdering his wife and suspected of being mentally sick, and it</span>
  <span id="freeText2562256966221177353" style="display:none">Although "Diamond Dust" remains my favourite Ahmed Mourad piece, this book, like all his other books, is outstanding! The language, like always, is capturing, and the plot is excellently written! In this book, Mourad takes us to the Al-Abbaseyya mental hospital in Cairo where Dr Yahia goes back to pursue his work after staying at home willingly for 5 years. He happens to meet an old friend, Sherif, who comes as a murderer accused of murdering his wife and suspected of being mentally sick, and it is for Yahia to determine whether he is to be punished by the law or not. In Sherif's apartment, Yahia discovers some strange tools and a photo of Bassma, Sherif's wife, with a tattoo on her body, and Lobna, Sherif's sister whom Yahia wanted to marry at some point but her brother refused, starts to reappear in his life. A breath-taking novel with an unexpected ending.</span>

  <span id="freeText9910212036808458458" style="display:none">This book started out brilliantly, I raced through 200 pages of a murder mystery starring a psychiatrist, book had the makings of a really psychiatric thriller with just the right dose of confusion, medical jargon and character insight. Yet the awesomeness came to a screeching halt after what was probably one of the best twists I have read in years (making it even more disappointing). The author decides to abandon the plausible and sensational line he had going in favour of some black magic, gen, myth and what not. Book rapidly deteriorates into a barrage of sex, drugs, alcohol and old wives tales. Really... really disappointing. Last 50 pages I read out of a feeling of duty in the hope he salvages it. Ending was horrid to top.</span>

<div id="review_1001496129" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1001496129" />
    <a title="Mervat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12966064-mervat"><img alt="Mervat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348059733p2/12966064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1001496129?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mervat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mervat" href="/user/show/12966064-mervat">Mervat</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1001496129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12766630477889017728">Ahmed Mourad puts so much detail and thought in his characters that he makes them so real. And that is one thing i like about his writing.<br/>However, this novel was a bit confusing for me, especially the long dream and the ending when the hero wakes up with a tattoo in his arms.. But, When i saw the movie, it cleared most of the vague events in the book. Nevertheless, the book was way better than the movie when describing the emotions of the characters.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

He -as usual- nailed the plot and kept me at the edge of my chair for most of the book.<br/><br/>27/8/2014<br/>Well after I figured this novel was not original I take back almost all my words....</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Mt/29YyQjRachIoLWUMG9g4oqiUKXpH3ceC8Nw8oSaQI+Z8nN85EfjuvPmqutgwp2HdN7cTTH5AqnvqGwmu7Pg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UNril35SEZB8OBWXXOPzuG2p/BJDOiA/yITVVaS2MuRq/ItFxQzY+NsTofarFvlnu/Yb2o23rliT+pPkafXAfg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText3004858909181932838" style="display:none">أحمد مراد.. <br />كاتب مصري من مواليد القاهرة 1978، تخرّج في مدرسة ليسيه الحرّية بباب اللوق عام 2006 قبل أن يلتحق بالمعهد العالي للسينما ليدرس التصوير السينمائي، وتخرّج عام 2001 بترتيب الأول على القسم، ونالت أفلام تخرّجه "الهائمون - الثلاث ورقات - وفي اليوم السابع" جوائز للأفلام القصيرة في مهرجانات بإنجلترا وفرنسا وأوكرانيا.. <br />بدأ أحمد كتابة روايته الأولي "فيرتيجو" في شتاء عام 2007، ونُشِرت في نفس العام عن دار "ميريت"، قبل أن تُترجم للّغة الإنجليزية عن دار "بلومزبيري"، ثم للإيطالية عن دار "مارسيليو"، والفرنسية عن دار "فلاماريون".. ثم تحولت الرواية لمسلسل تليفزيوني في رمضان من عام 2012.. <br />ثم أصدر أحمد روايته الثانية في فبراير 2010 بعنوان "تراب الماس" وتُرجمت للإيطالية عن دار "مارسيليو"، وأتبعها برواية "الفيل الأزرق" التي صدرت في أكتوبر من عام 2012.. </span>
